Grafana dashboard JSON model versioning and migration system is implemented across multiple Go source files in the apps/dashboard/pkg/migration directory.\\n\\nCore Migration Infrastructure:\\n- The main entry point is the Migrate() function in migrate.go, which orchestrates the entire migration process for a dashboard JSON object to a target schema version.\\n- The migrator struct manages a singleton pattern and stores a map of SchemaVersionMigrationFunc functions indexed by version number.\\n- The Initialize() function sets up the migrator with required dependencies, particularly the DataSourceInfoProvider.\\n\\nSchema Version Definitions and Registry:\\n- migrations.go defines the SchemaVersionMigrationFunc type as a function signature that takes context and a dashboard map.\\n- It defines MIN_VERSION (0) and LATEST_VERSION (42), establishing the migration range.\\n- The GetMigrations() function returns a map registry that associates each schema version (2-42) with its corresponding migration function.\\n- The GetSchemaVersion() utility extracts the current schema version from a dashboard JSON object, handling multiple data types (int, float64, string).\\n\\nData Source and Type Information:\\n- DataSourceInfoProvider interface defines GetDataSourceInfo() for retrieving datasource metadata.\\n- DataSourceInfo struct contains UID, Type, Name, ID, APIVersion, and Default flag.\\n- datasource_utils.go provides field-level migration utilities: GetDataSourceRef(), MigrateDatasourceNameToRef(), and GetDefaultDSInstanceSettings().\\n\\nField-Level Migration Functions:\\n- migration_utils.go contains utility functions for safe type conversion: GetStringValue(), GetBoolValue(), GetIntValue(), GetFloatValue(), ConvertToFloat(), and ConvertToInt().\\n- These utilities handle the JSON unmarshaling uncertainties where numeric values may come as float64, int, or string.\\n- datasource_utils.go implements the logic to convert datasource references from legacy string names to structured objects with uid, type, and apiVersion.\\n\\nVersion-Specific Migrations:\\n- All 41 migration versions (v2.go through v42.go) implement specific field and structure transformations.\\n- Notable migrations include:\\n  - V16: Converts from row-based layout to modern grid-based layout\\n  - V33: Migrates panel datasource references from strings to UIDs, taking a DataSourceInfoProvider and returning a SchemaVersionMigrationFunc\\n  - V36: Comprehensive datasource reference migration across annotations, template variables, and panels\\n- Each migration function follows the pattern of taking a context and dashboard map, modifying it in place, and returning an error.\\n\\nFrontend Defaults Application:\\n- frontend_defaults.go applies all DashboardModel and PanelModel constructor defaults before migrations run.\\n- This includes setting default values for title, tags, timezone, time range, panels array, and other dashboard properties.\\n- Panel defaults are applied including refId, fieldConfig, options, and transformations.\\n\\nError Handling:\\n- schemaversion/errors.go defines MigrationError type for schema migration errors and MinimumVersionError for dashboards below minimum migration version.\\n- NewMigrationError() and NewMinimumVersionError() factory functions create properly typed error instances.\\n- Error types include method GetFunctionName() to identify which migration step failed.\\n\\nAPI Version Conversion Layer:\\n- conversion/conversion.go registers K8s-style conversion functions between dashboard API versions (v0alpha1, v1beta1, v2alpha1, v2beta1).\\n- Conversion files (v0.go, v1.go, v2.go) implement Convert_V0_to_V1, Convert_V0_to_V2alpha1, etc. functions.\\n- These conversions invoke the Migrate() function to apply schema version migrations during API version transitions.\\n- conversion/errors.go defines ConversionError type separate from schema migration errors.\\n\\nMetrics and Monitoring:\\n- migration/metrics.go defines Prometheus counters for conversion success/failure with labels for source/target API versions and schema versions.\\n- conversion/metrics.go wraps conversions with withConversionMetrics() to track success/failure, error types, and dashboard UIDs.\\n\\nTest Utilities:\\n- testutil/mocks.go provides ConfigurableDataSourceProvider for testing with predefined datasource configurations (StandardTestConfig, DevDashboardConfig).\\n- testutil/utils.go provides helper functions for test execution and JSON file management.\\n\\nThe migration system works by: (1) applying frontend defaults to normalize the dashboard, (2) determining the input schema version, (3) iteratively running each migration function for versions between input and target, (4) updating the schemaVersion field after each step, and (5) cleaning up the dashboard to match the frontend save model format. This ensures that legacy Grafana dashboards can be reliably upgraded to current schema versions while maintaining data integrity and compatibility across Grafana instances.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1361,"cache_read_input_tokens":53268,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1361},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"55b7517b-daa4-401f-8874-3f9a252f638c","uuid":"7935cc60-3f78-4870-b792-fd43a6978394"}

Grafana dashboard JSON model versioning and migration system is implemented across multiple Go source files in the apps/dashboard/pkg/migration directory.\\n\\nCore Migration Infrastructure:\\n- The main entry point is the Migrate() function in migrate.go, which orchestrates the entire migration process for a dashboard JSON object to a target schema version.\\n- The migrator struct manages a singleton pattern and stores a map of SchemaVersionMigrationFunc functions indexed by version number.\\n- The Initialize() function sets up the migrator with required dependencies, particularly the DataSourceInfoProvider.\\n\\nSchema Version Definitions and Registry:\\n- migrations.go defines the SchemaVersionMigrationFunc type as a function signature that takes context and a dashboard map.\\n- It defines MIN_VERSION (0) and LATEST_VERSION (42), establishing the migration range.\\n- The GetMigrations() function returns a map registry that associates each schema version (2-42) with its corresponding migration function.\\n- The GetSchemaVersion() utility extracts the current schema version from a dashboard JSON object, handling multiple data types (int, float64, string).\\n\\nData Source and Type Information:\\n- DataSourceInfoProvider interface defines GetDataSourceInfo() for retrieving datasource metadata.\\n- DataSourceInfo struct contains UID, Type, Name, ID, APIVersion, and Default flag.\\n- datasource_utils.go provides field-level migration utilities: GetDataSourceRef(), MigrateDatasourceNameToRef(), and GetDefaultDSInstanceSettings().\\n\\nField-Level Migration Functions:\\n- migration_utils.go contains utility functions for safe type conversion: GetStringValue(), GetBoolValue(), GetIntValue(), GetFloatValue(), ConvertToFloat(), and ConvertToInt().\\n- These utilities handle the JSON unmarshaling uncertainties where numeric values may come as float64, int, or string.\\n- datasource_utils.go implements the logic to convert datasource references from legacy string names to structured objects with uid, type, and apiVersion.\\n\\nVersion-Specific Migrations:\\n- All 41 migration versions (v2.go through v42.go) implement specific field and structure transformations.\\n- Notable migrations include:\\n  - V16: Converts from row-based layout to modern grid-based layout\\n  - V33: Migrates panel datasource references from strings to UIDs, taking a DataSourceInfoProvider and returning a SchemaVersionMigrationFunc\\n  - V36: Comprehensive datasource reference migration across annotations, template variables, and panels\\n- Each migration function follows the pattern of taking a context and dashboard map, modifying it in place, and returning an error.\\n\\nFrontend Defaults Application:\\n- frontend_defaults.go applies all DashboardModel and PanelModel constructor defaults before migrations run.\\n- This includes setting default values for title, tags, timezone, time range, panels array, and other dashboard properties.\\n- Panel defaults are applied including refId, fieldConfig, options, and transformations.\\n\\nError Handling:\\n- schemaversion/errors.go defines MigrationError type for schema migration errors and MinimumVersionError for dashboards below minimum migration version.\\n- NewMigrationError() and NewMinimumVersionError() factory functions create properly typed error instances.\\n- Error types include method GetFunctionName() to identify which migration step failed.\\n\\nAPI Version Conversion Layer:\\n- conversion/conversion.go registers K8s-style conversion functions between dashboard API versions (v0alpha1, v1beta1, v2alpha1, v2beta1).\\n- Conversion files (v0.go, v1.go, v2.go) implement Convert_V0_to_V1, Convert_V0_to_V2alpha1, etc. functions.\\n- These conversions invoke the Migrate() function to apply schema version migrations during API version transitions.\\n- conversion/errors.go defines ConversionError type separate from schema migration errors.\\n\\nMetrics and Monitoring:\\n- migration/metrics.go defines Prometheus counters for conversion success/failure with labels for source/target API versions and schema versions.\\n- conversion/metrics.go wraps conversions with withConversionMetrics() to track success/failure, error types, and dashboard UIDs.\\n\\nTest Utilities:\\n- testutil/mocks.go provides ConfigurableDataSourceProvider for testing with predefined datasource configurations (StandardTestConfig, DevDashboardConfig).\\n- testutil/utils.go provides helper functions for test execution and JSON file management.\\n\\nThe migration system works by: (1) applying frontend defaults to normalize the dashboard, (2) determining the input schema version, (3) iteratively running each migration function for versions between input and target, (4) updating the schemaVersion field after each step, and (5) cleaning up the dashboard to match the frontend save model format. This ensures that legacy Grafana dashboards can be reliably upgraded to current schema versions while maintaining data integrity and compatibility across Grafana instances.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
